===== Page 145 =====
EXTRACT FROM LEGISLATIVE COUNCIL PROCEEDINGS
DATED THE 31ST OF MARCH, 1941.

MOTION BY THE ATTORNEY-GENERAL.

The Attorney-General: Sir, I move that this Council, in accordance with section 2(2) of the War Duties Ordinance, 1940, approves the extension of the operation of the said Ordinance for a further period of one year from the first day of April, 1941.

As Hon. Members will remember, this Ordinance, which was passed nearly a year ago, was expressed to remain in force for only one year but could be extended for further periods of one year by resolution of this Council.

I think probably most of the provisions of the Ordinance are not contentious, but it may save a certain amount of debate if I say at once that Government has decided that certain amendments to the Estate Duty Schedule should be made and legislation will be introduced at the next meeting of this Council on the 28th of April to give effect to that decision. It is not admitted that the rates as they stand are too high in themselves, but it is appreciated that in the circumstances of the Colony it might be difficult and might cause great hardship to have to realise substantial sums in cash by the realisation of property in a limited market such as we have in Malaya. It is therefore proposed to scale down the rates of estate duty, to make provision for the payment of estate duty by instalments on the lines of the English Finance Act, to reduce the rate of interest payable when estate duty is paid by instalments, and to provide that Government Bonds may be used in payment of estate duty at market value at the date when they are surrendered.

Hon. Members will realise that this involves not only an amendment of the Schedule to the Ordinance which we are now asking Council to renew, but will also necessitate substantive amendment of the Estate Duty Ordinance.

It has not been possible in the time available to prepare that Bill in time for the meeting today, but if this motion is passed today a Bill will be introduced at the next meeting on the 28th April to give effect to the decisions I have mentioned just now.

The Financial Secretary: Sir, I rise to second the motion.

Mr. J. I. Dawson: Sir, connected with this matter of War Duties is a question which has been raised in the market, i.e., whether or not the time is ripe for the raising of a further loan. The suggestion is that as the price today of the 3% War Loan stands at 103 it shows quite a premium even allowing for accrued interest, which seems to indicate that a good deal of money is lying idle awaiting investment. It is believed in responsible quarters that a loan of $10 million in the Colony would quickly be subscribed. It would, of course, be advisable to issue such loans in both the Federated Malay States and the Colony at the same time, but if that is not possible, it may be wise to raise one in the Colony only.

[P.T.O.]

===== Page 146 =====
Capt: N. M. Hashim: Sir, the brilliant success of the ever victorious British Imperial arms in Africa and around the Mediterranean, which has resulted in the liberation of races and countries in that part of the world from the tyranny and oppression of the ever treacherous and brutal Mussolini, and which has thereby assured the security and safety of Muslim Holy Lands in the Hedjaz from invasion by the destroyer of Islam and the head of the organised Fascist bandits, who cunningly calls himself "the Protector of Islam", and also in view of the establishment in England of the headquarters of all the Nazi-held European countries that have been ruthlessly occupied and looted, the defensive war of the Commonwealth of British Nations for the protection of mankind, freedom and civilisation, has unconsciously been transformed into the defensive war of the Commonwealth of Free Nations, in spite of Marshal Pétain's disagreement with the formation of a Franco-British Union on the suggestion of Mr. Winston Churchill, just before the collapse of France. This natural evolution will be inevitable, especially after the hammer-like smashing blows which the Nazi-Fascists will eventually receive in the Balkans on their own seeking due to their continual aggression and lust for power, their greed and brutal plundering and looting of territories and properties in excelsis, and the bleeding and fleeing of the people, leaving them exhausted and starving.

To assess the degree of inhumanity committed by the Italians during their occupation of Abyssinia for the last five years, one has only to consider the fear now disclosed by Mussolini of Abyssinian reprisals against the 200,000 Italian settlers when Addis Ababa falls, as fall it must. The ghosts of their past misdeeds are now haunting them.

What about the imposition of an annual toll of 3,150 millions on Norway, Denmark, Belgium, Holland and France by Hitler, in addition to the booty already bagged for the privilege of being occupied by the German army? The toll on Norway and France represents between one-quarter and one-third of their pre-occupation income.

I say that the transformation to a Commonwealth of Free Nations is inevitable because of the sound basis of justice, freedom and liberty on which the original nucleus, namely, the British Empire has been built up. Every nation, whether within the fold or not, is at full liberty, without any compulsion whatsoever, to live and act according to the dictates of its religious, racial, cultural and political inclinations, as decided by the competent authority of the sons of the soil. As an illustration, I quote (1) Ireland, which has always been, and still is, in the fold, and which has decided to remain neutral during this war. She is up to this day a neutral country with the Nazis' representative quite comfortable on her soil. The Commonwealth simply says, "Well, we will come to your help whenever you need that help for your safety". (2) The Dominion of South Africa which joined the war only on the majority vote of her Cabinet. (3) The United States of America, one of the biggest, strongest, most enlightened and independent countries in the world, which has never been in the fold, but which, with the passing of the Lease and Lend Bill, has partially supported the Commonwealth of Free Nations.

Today's defensive war against the world's enemies for the salvation of mankind peace has thereby - and again unconsciously - been transformed from one of National to one of Free Peoples.

One of the great policies of the British Commonwealth, in fact, it has become its trait, is that, under no circumstances whatsoever, will it give up any part of the land in the Commonwealth to any other than the sons of the soil who have lived on the land and owned it. (The Governor: Hear, hear).

===== Page 147 =====
I should, therefore, not be at all surprised if after the crushing defeat of the aggressors in Europe and the Middle East and the settlement of outstanding questions in the Far East, when every people concerned has become sober and realised the right of every other people or race, there emerges a great Commonwealth of Free Peoples in the world. I am hopeful and optimistic. The present chaos is only one of the many that have appeared in the past from time to time - a blessing in disguise - and which have resulted in the world emerging into a better one than previously. Surely, bar the present turmoil, the world of to-day is better than that of the past. It is only a question of handling the present situation faithfully, sincerely and courageously.

In addition to continual specious pretexts, designed and advanced by the Axis, in accordance with their usual method of masking their ulterior aggressive aims, the work of their "fifth-column" agencies is notoriously well-known throughout the world. Every means and device are unceasingly and cunningly employed to undermine and wreck every country or people or section of people whether in the defensive warring countries or not.

On the authority of Reuter and the reports of individuals too reliable and acceptable to need any quotation or reference, it is known throughout the world that their propaganda is too glaring and superfluous to be believed.

We, too, realise that our country with its floating population of various races and the insidious influence of foreign elements is not immune from the attempts of the "fifth column" schemes of the Axis. The Honourable the Legal Adviser, F.M.S., was reported to have made a reference at a meeting of the Federal Council to the existence of communistic elements in the country. There is a lot in what he said and, irrespective of the quarters from which suggestions detrimental to our cause or activities have come without our knowing their origins and their ulterior motives, we have to be cautious in considering them.

At the meeting of this Council in January this year I appealed for information regarding the activities of the authorities in respect of the preparation for defending this important outpost of the Empire. I daresay the intelligent public are satisfied and grateful with the enlightenment they have since received.

In addition to the varied information already given by the authorities, there is a certain bit of information which I feel it my duty to let out. When the Compulsory Military Training Bill was passed by this Council, a letter appeared in the Press enquiring what section of the community a certain member of this Council could claim to represent. When the War Tax Bill on incomes and profits was passed, similar voices were also heard here and there. I don't blame these enquirers. What they need is enlightenment. In a sense the statement was correct. Every one of us in this Council represents to-day something more than any sectional community. The war has removed all sectional divisions and made us, as never before, a united family. We all realise that unity must be our watchword and that the preservation of a national existence, nay life itself, depends on concerted action. These are grave times. Grave, however, as they are, we can still face the future with confidence, but only on one condition, that is, if with quiet efficiency, unflinching courage and unceasing determination we have but one aim and purpose: to unite, as never before, in the face of our ruthless foes. This is not the time for considering how we are to do it. We must make up our minds what is to be done and then do it quickly, boldly and whole-heartedly.

Money

P.T.O.

===== Page 148 =====
Money is needed for the defence of this country against the insatiable vultures. This War Duties Ordinance of 1940 provides one of the means of getting the money needed. It has been proposed and seconded to extend the operation of this Ordinance for a further period of one year from the 1st day of April, 1941, and I support it. (Applause).

The Financial Secretary: Sir, the Hon. Mr. DAWSON's plea for a further War Loan gives me the opportunity of stating that the matter is already under consideration by Government, and I am therefore grateful to him for having brought it up at this meeting. (Applause).

The motion was agreed to.

An Enactment for imposing additional taxation for War purposes.

T. S. W. THOMAS,
President of the Federal Council.

[21st February, 1941.]

WHEREAS it is desirable to impose additional taxation for the purpose of contributing towards the expenses incurred in the prosecution of the present war:

It is hereby enacted by the Rulers of the Federated Malay States by and with the advice and consent of the Federal Council as follows:

PART I.

PRELIMINARY.

1. This Enactment may be cited as the War Taxation Enactment, 1941, and shall have effect as from the 1st day of January, 1941.

2. In this Enactment unless there is something repugnant in the subject or context:

"Accountant-General" means the Accountant-General of the Federated Malay States;

"Annual value" means

(a) in the case of land let to a tenant otherwise than as provided in paragraph (b), the gross amount of rent actually received, including any fine, premium or foregift demanded and given in connection with such letting;

(b) in the case of land let to a tenant where, in consideration of improvements made or to be made at the cost of the tenant or for other specific cause, the rent reserved is less than the gross amount at which it could reasonably be expected to let, the gross amount at which it could reasonably be expected to let;

(c) in the case of land occupied by the owner or let free of rent, the gross amount at which it could reasonably be expected to let,

the landlord in each case paying the expenses of repair, insurance, maintenance or upkeep and all Sanitary Board rates;

"Auditor" means the Auditor of the Federated Malay States;

===== Page 153 =====
"net annual value" means the annual value less
(a) the amount actually paid by the landlord as Sanitary Board rates; and
(b) a sum equal to one-eighth of the annual value in respect of the expenses of repair, insurance, maintenance and upkeep unless such expenses are payable by the tenant;

"association" means any firm, and any society or body or association of persons, whether incorporated or not, other than a company and includes what in any system of law prevailing in India is known as a Hindu Joint Family or co-parcenary;

"British Empire" means the United Kingdom of Great Britain and Northern Ireland, the Dominions, India, Burma, the territories administered by His Britannic Majesty’s Governments in the Dominions under Mandate or otherwise, the British Colonies, the British Protectorates and Protected States, and the Mandated Territories of Tanganyika, the Cameroons under British Mandate and Togoland under British Mandate;

"business" includes profession, vocation, trade, manufacture, adventure, undertaking and concern;

"charge", "charge" and "chargee" have the same meaning as in the Land Code;

"company" means an association of persons carrying on business in the Federated Malay States whose capital is divided into shares or stock and transferable, whether the company is incorporated or not, and whether its principal place of business is situated in the Federated Malay States or not, and includes any company incorporated in the Federated Malay States;

"defaulter" includes a company or association making default under this Enactment;

"dividend" includes any distribution made by a company to its shareholders, whether in money or other property, out of its profits, and the paid-up value of shares distributed by a company to its shareholders to the extent to which the paid-up value represents the capitalisation of the whole or any part of the profits of the company, but does not include a reversionary bonus on a policy of life assurance;

"financial year" means each period of twelve months at the end of which the balance of the accounts is struck or, if no such balance is struck, then the year from the 1st day of January to the 31st day of December both days inclusive;

"income" includes
(i) in the case of a company, other than a life assurance company, incorporated in the Federated Malay States,
(a) the total net profits of its business wheresoever made;
(b) the net annual value of lands, owned by it wheresoever the same may be situated;
(c) interest from any source, whether within or without the Federated Malay States;

===== Page 154 =====
(d) dividends, profits, commissions, or bonuses credited or paid by any company, association, or person whether within or without the Federated Malay States;

(e) its income from any other source wheresoever arising:

(ii) in the case of a life assurance company incorporated in the Federated Malay States, the whole of its income from investments less the management expenses and commission:

(iii) in the case of a company, other than a life assurance company, which is not incorporated in the Federated Malay States or of an association,

(a) the net profits of its business arising or received in the Federated Malay States;

(b) the net annual value of lands owned by it and situated in the Federated Malay States;

(c) interest from any source arising or received in the Federated Malay States;

(d) dividends, profits, commissions, or bonuses credited or paid by any company, association, or person arising or received in the Federated Malay States;

(e) its income from any other source arising or received in the Federated Malay States:

(iv) in the case of a life assurance company, which is not incorporated in the Federated Malay States,

(a) the net profits of its business arising or received in the Federated Malay States; and

(b) an amount equal to ten per centum of the amount, if any, set aside for, credited or distributed to, holders of policies issued in the Federated Malay States in the way of bonus, abatement of premium or addition to the sum insured; or

(c) in lieu of (a) and (b) at the option of the Collector, the interest or profits on its investments in the Federated Malay States and from any other source arising or received in the Federated Malay States:

(v) in the case of an individual

(a) the net profits, derived by him from carrying on any business, arising or received in the Federated Malay States;

(b) the net annual value of lands owned by him and situated in the Federated Malay States;

(c) interest from any source arising or received in or brought into the Federated Malay States;

(d) dividends, profits, commissions or bonuses credited or paid by any company, association, or person arising or received in or brought into the Federated Malay States;

===== Page 155 =====
(e) salary arising or received in or brought into the Federated Malay States;
(f) his income from any other source arising or received in or brought into the Federated Malay States;

"income tax" includes any tax levied on the basis of income;

"land" has the same meaning as in the Land Code;

"monthly salary" means the amount which is due and payable to any person in respect of any month during which he is employed and which consists of such portion of his salary as the employer has agreed to pay to such person at regular intervals and at an agreed amount;

"pension" includes annuity and gratuity (other than any capital sum received by way of retiring gratuity or in commutation of the whole or any part of a pension);

"principal officer" includes
(a) the Secretary, Treasurer, Manager or Agent of any company or association;
(b) any person connected with a company or association upon whom the Collector has served a notice of his intention to treat him as the principal officer thereof;

"salary" includes
(a) allowances [other than travelling allowances considered to be reasonable by the Collector], fees, commissions, bonuses, gratuities and perquisites or profits credited, set aside or received in lieu of or in addition to a fixed salary, in respect of an office or employment of profit; and
(b) the value of any food, clothing or lodging provided or paid for by the employer; and
(c) the annual value of any place of residence provided rent-free by the employer; and
(d) where a place of residence is provided by an employer at a rent less than the annual value, the excess of the annual value over such rent:
Provided that for the purposes of paragraphs (c) and (d) of this definition if the annual value is in excess of ten per centum of salary from other sources such excess shall be disregarded;

"Sanitary Board rates" includes education rate;

"total income" means
(i) in the case of a company, incorporated in the Federated Malay States, its income;
(ii) in the case of a company, other than a life assurance company, which is not incorporated in the Federated Malay States, or of an association,
(a) the total net profits of its business wheresoever made;
(b) the net annual value of lands owned by it wheresoever the same may be situated;
(c) interest from any source, whether within or without the Federated Malay States.

===== Page 156 =====
WAR TAXATION.

(d) Dividends, profits, commissions or bonuses credited or paid by any company, association or person whether within or without the Federated Malay States;

(e) Its income from any other source wheresoever arising:

(iii) In the case of a life assurance company, not incorporated in the Federated Malay States,

(a) The net profits of its business wheresoever made, and

(b) An amount equal to ten per centum of the amount, if any, set aside for, credited or distributed to policy holders in the way of bonus, abatement of premium or addition to the sum insured; or

(c) In lieu of (a) and (b) at the option of the Collector the interest or profits on its investments wheresoever arising:

(iv) In the case of an individual

(a) The total net profits, derived by him from carrying on any business, wheresoever made;

(b) The net annual value of lands owned by him wheresoever the same may be situated;

(c) Interest from any source wheresoever arising;

(d) Dividends, profits, commissions or bonuses credited or paid by any company, association or person whether within or without the Federated Malay States;

(e) His salary wheresoever arising excluding messing and lodging allowances paid by Government or by the Government of the Straits Settlements to members of any of the armed forces of those Governments when called up for continuous training;

(f) His income from any other source wheresoever arising:

Provided that in any of these cases any sum paid in respect of Income Tax or of any tax specially imposed for the purposes of the present war in any part of the British Empire or of any tax under this Enactment shall be deemed to form part of total income.

PART II.

OFFICERS, ETC.

3. (1) The High Commissioner may by notification in the Gazette establish such Divisions in the Federated Malay States as he thinks necessary.

(2) The High Commissioner may appoint for the whole of the Federated Malay States or for any such Division a Collector and such number of Assistant Collectors as he may think necessary for the purpose of assessing, collecting, receiving and accounting for the tax and of giving effect generally to the provisions of this Enactment.

===== Page 157 =====
(3) The High Commissioner may also appoint a Collector-General under whose directions the Collectors shall act.

(4) The High Commissioner may also appoint Assessors to advise the Collectors in fixing assessments.

4. All or any of the powers and duties conferred or imposed by this Enactment on a Collector or the Collector-General may be exercised or performed by such other person as the High Commissioner may appoint in this behalf.

PART III.

LIABILITY TO TAX.

5. Subject to the provisions of this Enactment there shall be paid for the year commenced the 1st day of January, 1941, to the Government in respect of the income of every company association or person assessed as hereinafter provided a war tax (hereinafter called "the tax") at the rate specified in the Schedule to this Enactment as appropriate to the total income of the company, association or person chargeable with the tax.

6. (1) The incomes of the following Governments, Boards, authorities and persons shall be exempt from liability to the tax under this Enactment and from the liability to make a return under section 12 thereof:

(a) the Government of the Straits Settlements or of any Unfederated Malay State;

(b) the Board administering the Fund created under the Public Officers Guarantee Fund Enactment;

(c) the Public Trustee Investment Board constituted under the Public Trustee Enactment;

(d) the Board of the Rubber Research Institute constituted under the Rubber Research Institute of Malaya Enactment;

(e) the Planters' Loans Board constituted under the Planters' Loans Fund Enactment;

(f) the Indian Immigration Committee constituted under the Labour Code in respect of the Indian Immigration Fund constituted under the said Code and thereunder vested in the said Committee;

(g) the Controller of Rubber and the Advisory Committee appointed under the Rubber Regulation Enactment 1936 in respect of the Malayan Rubber Fund which they control and administer;

(h) the Accountant-General in respect of moneys and investments held by him for the Savings Bank in accordance with the provisions of the Post Office Savings Bank Enactment 1936;

(i) the Trustees of the Selangor King George V Silver Jubilee Fund constituted under the Selangor King George V Silver Jubilee Enactment 1937;

(j) any company, association or person whose total income is less than $4,800 a year; and

(k) any other bodies or classes of persons declared from time to time by Resolution of the Federal Council published in the Gazette to be exempt from liability to the tax and to assessment under this Enactment.

===== Page 158 =====
(2) The exemption under this section shall be limited to the Governments, Boards, authorities and persons herein referred to and shall not extend to the salaries of persons employed by them, although such salaries may be paid wholly or in part out of the incomes so exempt, nor shall such exemption extend to moneys paid to other companies, associations or persons out of the funds of such Governments, Boards, authorities or persons.

7. In calculating the income on which a company, association or person shall pay the tax, a deduction shall be made in respect of the following:

(a) such portion of the income of any religious, educational or charitable company or association as is solely employed for religious, educational or charitable purposes within the Federated Malay States;

(b) any income on which income-tax has been paid or on which it is proved to the satisfaction of the Collector income-tax will be paid in any other part of the British Empire at a rate not less than the rate specified in the Schedule;

(c) any income derived by a cultivator of rubber or a miner of tin-ore from rubber or tin-ore produced or mined by such cultivator or miner as to which it is proved to the satisfaction of the Collector that there has been levied thereon and paid an export duty specially imposed for the purposes of the present war by any written law of the Federated Malay States or of the Colony or of any Unfederated Malay State or that such rubber or tin-ore is exempt from payment of such duty by reason of any provision of any such written law;

(d) any income derived from interest paid in respect of any loan raised in the Federated Malay States or in any other part of the British Empire for the prosecution of the present war;

(e) the official salary of a consular officer who is not a British subject and does not carry on business in the Federated Malay States: Provided that reciprocal treatment is accorded by the country of such consular officer to British consular officers;

(f) the allowances paid from Navy, Army or Air Force funds to any officer, non-commissioned officer or man of His Britannic Majesty's Forces;

(g) any income which a company, association or person enjoys as a member of a company or association when the company or association is liable to the tax;

(h) such portion of the income of any person as is deducted by the Government as a contribution under the Widows and Orphans Pension Enactment or under any similar written law in force in any other part of the British Empire, or is deducted by any employer as a contribution to a provident fund recognized by the Federal Secretary; and such portion as is paid by such person to a life assurance

===== Page 159 =====
company in respect of any insurance effected for the purpose of securing for himself or his wife or wives or any of his children either a provision or a deferred annuity:

Provided that the amount or the aggregate of the amounts allowed to be deducted under this paragraph from the income of any person shall not exceed one-sixth of such income;

(i) such travelling allowances as may be considered reasonable by the Collector;

(j) such sum as the Collector may think just and reasonable as representing the diminished value by reason of wear and tear of any machinery or plant used for the purposes of any business;

(k) such part of the interest paid on borrowed capital as bears taxation imposed under this Enactment or is exempt from taxation under the provisions of paragraph (b) of this section;

(l) such portion of any dividend received from a company or income enjoyed as a member of an association engaged in the production of rubber or tin as is shown to the satisfaction of the Collector to have been derived from income in respect of which such company or association is entitled to a deduction under the provisions of paragraph (c) of this section;

(m) the net annual value of any lands situated in the Federated Malay States as are shown to the satisfaction of the Collector to be owned and occupied by the company, association or person and used exclusively for the purposes of any business carried on by it or him.

8. A deduction shall not, in any case, be made in respect of the following matters:

(a) money not wholly and exclusively laid out or expended for the purposes of the business carried on by a company, association or person;

(b) any loss or expense which is recoverable under any contract of insurance or indemnity;

(c) any sums credited or paid as salaries by any association to any of its members, or any sums drawn by, credited to or set aside for the benefit of such members;

(d) any loss not connected with or arising out of any business, or any capital withdrawn from any business, or any loss or expenditure of a capital nature, or any sum used or intended to be used as capital in any business;

(e) any capital used in the improvement of premises occupied for the purpose of any business;

(f) any sum exceeding two-thirds of the rent of any premises used partly as a dwelling and partly for the purposes of business;

===== Page 160 =====
(g) Any part of the annual value of premises used for the purpose of business where such premises belong to the company, association or person carrying on the business, and are situated outside the Federated Malay States.

(h) Any expenses of maintenance of the persons liable to the tax, their families or establishments, or any sum expended in any other domestic or private purpose.

(i) Any sum written off for depreciation of land, buildings or leases.

(j) Any sum expended for the supply or repairs or alterations of any implements, utensils or articles employed for the purposes of any business in excess of the average so expended in the last three financial years.

(k) Any interest which might have been earned on any capital if lent out at interest: Provided that the Collector shall allow the deduction of interest actually paid in respect of loans for the purposes of current business but not for use as capital except as provided in section 7(k) at a rate not higher than eight per centum per annum.

(l) Any bad debts, except bad debts proved to be such to the satisfaction of the Collector and to have been incurred in and actually written off in the year of assessment:

Provided that all amounts received during the year of assessment on account of any bad debts incurred prior to the year of assessment shall be credited to income in the year of assessment and shall, subject to the other provisions of this Enactment, be chargeable with the tax.

And Provided also that bad debts incurred in the financial year preceding the year of assessment and not proved to be bad and written off until the year of assessment may be deducted if the Collector considers that they would have been deductible if they had been proved to be bad and actually written off in the year of assessment.

And Provided Further that if it is shown to the satisfaction of the Collector that in any business the annual provision or some portion of the annual provision made to cover bad debts written off each year represents the equivalent of the amount that would be allowable as a deduction under this paragraph then the amount of such annual provision or such portion thereof as the Collector considers fairly represents the equivalent of the allowable deduction may be allowed as the deduction under this paragraph.

(m) Any sum paid as tax under this Enactment or as income tax in any country on any income arising in the Federated Malay States.

===== Page 161 =====
Part IV.
ASSESSMENT AND COLLECTION.
A.—Salaries and Pensions.

9. (1) Every employer shall on or before the 15th day of March, 1941, deliver to the Collector a return in the prescribed form showing
(a) the name of every person who at the date of the return is receiving or who during any part of the year 1941 prior to such date has received from him any salary or pension;
(b) the address of each such person;
(c) the amount of such salary or pension or the basis on which any unascertained portion of such salary is to be calculated;
(d) the date or dates on which such salary or pension becomes payable or was paid;
(e) the amount of salary or pension received by and the period for which such salary or pension was paid to each such person since the 1st day of January, 1941.

(2) Where an employer, who has not previously employed others in his service, commences so to employ any person after the 15th day of March, 1941, such employer shall within one month of the commencement of such employment make a return in the prescribed form to the Collector in respect of every person who enters his employment.

(3) Every employer shall as occasion arises notify the Collector when any person included in a return delivered under either sub-section (1) or sub-section (2) leaves his employment or the Federated Malay States or is transferred from one place of employment to another within the Federated Malay States, and shall also deliver to the Collector a return in the prescribed form in respect of any person who enters his employment after the date of a return delivered under either sub-section (1) or sub-section (2) or who after such date receives an increased or reduced salary or pension.

(4) Unless so required by the Collector, such returns need not include any person who is in receipt of a salary or pension of less than three hundred and fifty dollars per mensem and who has no other employment, and nil returns need not be delivered.

10. (1) Every employer shall, when he pays or credits to or sets aside for the benefit of any person any monthly salary or pension, deduct therefrom the proportionate part of the tax, if any, which would be payable under this Enactment in respect of the monthly salary or pension paid and to be paid to such person during the year if such monthly salary or pension formed such person's total income.

(2) Every employer shall, when he pays or credits to or sets aside for the benefit of any person any portion of that person's salary other than monthly salary deduct therefrom an amount equal to eight per centum of such portion of such salary.

(3) Every employer who did not make in the month of January 1941 any deduction such as is referred to in sub-sections (1) and (2) shall deduct such amount from any salary or pension

===== Page 162 =====
which he subsequently pays or credits to or sets aside during any subsequent month of the year 1941 and this deduction shall be additional to any other deduction then lawfully made: Provided that if any such additional deduction is made from monthly salary such additional deduction shall not exceed one-eleventh of the amount which is otherwise deducted from such monthly salary.

(4) Notwithstanding anything contained in sub-sections (1), (2) and (3), an employer shall not make any deduction under this section from any salary or pension paid, credited to or set aside for the benefit of any person not resident in the Federated Malay States unless the Collector so directs; and in any case where an employer is required under this section to make any deduction the Collector may at the request or with the consent of the person from whose salary or pension such deduction is required to be made direct the employer not to make such deduction or to make such deduction as may be specified by the Collector.

(5) Every employer shall within the prescribed time after such deduction pay the amount thereof to the Collector who shall thereupon credit such amount to the person from whose salary or pension it has been deducted as a credit against the amount of tax to which such person is or may become liable in respect of the year 1941.

(6) Any employer who fails to make any deduction referred to in this section may and at the request of the Collector shall deduct it when he subsequently pays any salary or pension to the person who is liable to the tax.

(7) The power of the employer to deduct under this section shall not prejudice any right of the Collector to recover the tax by other means.

(8) For the purposes of this section the word “salary” does not include any salary paid to an association or to a company.

11. (1) Every charger of land in the Federated Malay States may deduct from his income and total income for the purpose of assessment of the tax the amount of interest paid by him to his chargee: Provided that the amount deducted shall not exceed the net annual value of the property charged.

(2) Every charger of land in the Federated Malay States shall be deemed to be within the meaning of section 22 of this Enactment a person who receives on behalf of his chargee the interest payable by him to his chargee, unless there is some other person in the Federated Malay States authorized by such chargee to receive such interest.

C.— PROFITS OF COMPANIES AND ASSOCIATIONS.

12. (1) Except where a company or an association is carrying on a business newly set up or commenced on or after the 1st day of January, 1940, every company and every association whose income is not exempted from taxation under paragraph (j) of sub-section (1) of section 6 or whose income does not fall wholly within paragraph (b) or paragraph (c) of section 7 or wholly within paragraphs (b) and (c) of section 7 shall on or before the 30th day of June, 1941, deliver to the Collector a true

===== Page 163 =====
Statement in writing signed by its principal officer of its income and total income during its last financial year prior to the 1st day of April, 1941, and of the manner in which they have been calculated.

(2) Every company and every association which is carrying on a business newly set up or commenced during the year 1940, and whose income does not fall wholly within paragraph (b) or paragraph (c) of section 7 or wholly within paragraphs (b) and (c) of section 7 shall, within three months after completing a period of twelve months’ trading, deliver to the Collector a true statement in writing, signed by its principal officer, of its income and total income during such period and of the manner in which they have been calculated.

(3) Every company and every association which sets up or commences a business during the year 1941, and whose income does not fall wholly within paragraph (b) or paragraph (c) of section 7 or wholly within paragraphs (b) and (c) of section 7 shall on or before the 31st day of March, 1942, deliver to the Collector a true statement in writing signed by its principal officer of its income and total income during the year 1941, and of the manner in which they have been calculated: Provided that the Collector-General may at any time before the 31st day of March, 1942, agree with the company or association for a composition of the tax upon such terms as he may think fit.

(4) Such statement as is required by sub-section (1), (2) or (3), when made by a company incorporated in the Federated Malay States or in the Colony or in any Unfederated Malay State shall if the Collector so requires be certified by auditors approved by the Federal Secretary.

D.—INCOME GENERALLY.

13. (1) Every person who was during the year 1940 or who has reason to believe that during the year 1941 he may be in receipt of a total income amounting to four thousand eight hundred dollars per annum or more shall in the month of April 1941 notify the Collector in the prescribed form that he is chargeable with the tax, and shall in such notification state if he claims to be assessed at a lower rate than eight per centum.

(2) The Collector shall then send to each such person the appropriate forms prescribed for declaration of income and total income.

(3) Every such person shall within the prescribed time after such forms have been sent to it or him make thereon a full and accurate return of its or his income and total income, sign them and deliver them to the Collector.

14. The Collector shall from time to time determine what companies, associations and persons are chargeable with the tax and the rate and amount at which every such company, association and person is to be assessed.

15. The assessment shall be made
(a) as regards salaries or pensions and
(b) as regards income derived from carrying on a business newly set up or commenced or from land newly acquired on or after the 1st day of January, 1941 on the income received and to be received by the company association or person in the year 1941;

===== Page 164 =====
(c) As regards income derived from carrying on a business newly set up or commenced during the year 1940, or from land newly acquired during the year 1940, on the income received by the company, association or person during a period of twelve months calculated from the date of such commencement or acquisition.

(d) As regards the income of any company, association or person to which paragraphs (a), (b) and (c) do not apply.

(e) As regards income derived from any other sources on the income received by the company, association or person during its or his last financial year prior to the 1st day of April, 1941.

(f) As regards income derived by a company, association or person from carrying on a business or from the ownership of land in respect of which there has been a succession after the 31st day of December, 1940.

(g) As regards income derived from carrying on a business or from the ownership of land by an association in respect of which any change shall have taken place among the members either by death or dissolution of partnership as to all or any of the members thereof, or by the admission of any other member therein, after the 31st day of December, 1940 on the income of the business or property received during its or his last financial year prior to the 1st day of April, 1941, notwithstanding such succession to such business or property or change therein as aforesaid, unless such company, association or person shall prove to the satisfaction of the Collector that the income of such business or property has diminished or will diminish from a specific cause to be alleged by it or him since such succession or change took place or by reason thereof.

16. (1) In the case of a company, association or person selling goods in the Federated Malay States on account of a company, association or person whose principal place of business is not situated in the Federated Malay States, the company, association or person on whose account such goods are sold shall, if the income cannot otherwise be ascertained to the satisfaction of the Collector, be deemed to have derived from such sale an income to be determined by the Collector at a figure not exceeding the equivalent of five per centum of the price at which the goods were sold.

(2) Goods shall be deemed to be sold in the Federated Malay States under sub-section (1) if any company, association or person in the Federated Malay States receives a commission in respect of the sale of the goods or is paid a salary for obtaining orders for or for influencing the sale of the goods.

(3) The assessment shall be made:
(a) In the case of a business newly set up or commenced during the year 1941, on the income deemed to have been derived in the year 1941;
(b) In the case of a business newly set up or commenced during the year 1940, on the income deemed to have been derived during a period of twelve months from the date of such commencement.

===== Page 165 =====
(c) In other cases, on the income deemed to have been derived during the last financial year.

(4) Every company, association or person selling goods under sub-section (1) shall make to the Collector a true and full return of the amount for which the goods have been sold and when so required by the Collector, a true statement of the total income of the company, association or person on whose account the goods have been sold.

17. (1) Where the Collector in his discretion considers

(a) that the income or total income of any company, association or person cannot be readily ascertained or

(b) that the accounts of any company, association or person have not been kept in a satisfactory form or manner,

the Collector and two or more Assessors may compute the income and total income of any such company, association or person on the basis of the usual rate of net profit on the turnover of the trade or business carried on by such company, association or person or on such other basis as such Collector and Assessors consider reasonable. Such usual rate of profit shall be either as prescribed or shall be determined by such Collector and Assessors.

(2) If the Collector is satisfied that any company or association has been formed or that any device has been employed by any company, association or person for the purpose of enabling any company, association or person to pay less tax than he or it would otherwise be liable to pay under this Enactment, the Collector, after taking the advice of two or more Assessors, may determine the amount of tax which such company, association or person ought to pay as if any such first mentioned company or association had not been formed or such device had not been employed.

18. Notwithstanding the provisions of sub-section (1) of section 6 or of section 12, every company, association or person shall, when required by the Collector, furnish in the form required by him a statement or return or, where a statement or return has already been furnished, a further or fuller statement or return of income or total income in respect either of the whole or of any part of the income or total income received by such company, association or person, whether on its or his own behalf or in any of the capacities mentioned in sections 21, 22, 23, 24, 25 and 26.

19. (1) If the Collector is dissatisfied with any statement or return delivered to him under section 12, 13, 15 or 18, he may serve on the company, association or person a notice requiring its principal officer or him to attend at the Collector’s Office on a date therein mentioned and support the figures of its statement or his return and to produce or to cause to be produced all such of its or his accounts as refer to the year to which the statement or return relates and as are in its or his possession or power.

(2) On the day mentioned in the notice or as soon afterwards as may be, the Collector shall determine the amount at which such company, association or person is to be assessed.

===== Page 166 =====
(3) If the company, association or person fails to attend at the Collector's Office in pursuance of the notice served under sub-section (1), or if no statement or return is delivered to the Collector under section 12, 13, 15 or 18, the Collector after taking the advice of two or more Assessors may determine to the best of his judgment and ability the amount at which the company, association or person is to be assessed.

20. (1) The Collector shall as soon as he has assessed the amount of the tax with which a company, association or person is chargeable notify it or him, and it or he shall, unless it or he has presented a petition under section 30, within the prescribed time pay to the Collector such assessed amount, less any sums that have been paid or will be paid to the Collector under section 10 or under sub-section (2) of this section.

(2) The Collector may require any Government officer or other person whose duty it is to pay interest to any person in respect of any Government or other public loan or of any issue of debentures or of any other security bearing interest to deduct before paying such interest an amount equal to eight per centum of such interest and to pay to the Collector the amount so deducted: such Government officer or other person shall thereupon make such deduction and pay the amount thereof to the Collector who shall upon receiving such amount credit it to the person to whom such interest is due against any tax that may be payable by such person under this Enactment in respect of the year 1941.

E.—Trustees, Etc.

21. Every company which or person who acts as trustee, guardian, or committee of another person being an infant or a mentally disordered person and has control of the property of such other person whether such other person resides in the Federated Malay States or not shall

(a) be chargeable in the like manner and to the like amount as such other person would be chargeable if he did not suffer from any incapacity;

(b) be itself or himself liable to perform the duties which such other person would be required to perform under this Enactment if he did not suffer from any incapacity; and

(c) be subject to the penalties prescribed for a breach of such duties:

Provided that where two or more persons act as trustees, guardians, or committees of one such other person, they may notify the Collector in writing signed by them that they have elected one of themselves to be so chargeable and so liable under the Enactment and thereafter, if the Collector signifies his consent to such election, the person so elected shall alone be so chargeable and so liable.

In this section the expression "mentally disordered person" means any person found by due course of law to be of unsound mind and incapable of managing himself or his affairs.

22. (1) Every person who in any capacity not referred to in section 21 receives or holds as trustee, agent, manager or otherwise on behalf of any company, association or person carrying on business or resident in the Federated Malay States any income

===== Page 167 =====
liable to the tax shall, when so required by the Collector, declare to him the title, name, and place of business or abode of such company, association, or person and the amount of income so received.

(2) Any person in the Federated Malay States who, in any capacity not referred to in section 21, receives on behalf of another person not resident in the Federated Malay States, or pays or credits to any person not resident in the Federated Malay States any income liable to the tax, shall deduct therefrom the tax at the rate of eight per centum and shall, within the prescribed time, pay the sum deducted to the Collector as a credit against the amount of tax to which such person is or may become liable in respect of the year 1941.

23. Every person who receives or holds on behalf of a company or association, whose principal place of business is not situated in the Federated Malay States, and every company or association which receives or holds on behalf of any person who is resident outside the Federated Malay States or of another company or association whose principal place of business is not situated within the Federated Malay States, any income liable to the tax shall deduct therefrom the tax at the rate of eight per centum and shall, within the prescribed time, pay the sum deducted to the Collector as a credit against the amount of tax to which such person is or may become liable in respect of the year 1941.

24. Any receiver or manager appointed by any Court in the Federated Malay States shall be chargeable in respect of all income in his possession or under his control as such receiver or manager.

25. Where any person liable to the tax dies, or where the estate of a deceased person is being administered, the executors, administrators, trustees, and all persons having control, management, or custody of the income of such deceased person or of his estate shall each and every one of them, in respect of the income within his control, management or custody:

(a) be chargeable in the like manner and to the like amount as such deceased person would be chargeable if he were alive;

(b) be liable to perform the duties which such deceased person would be required to perform under this Enactment if he were alive; and

(c) be subject to the penalties prescribed for any breach of such duties.

26. Where any person has not made full and complete returns during his lifetime and has thereby escaped full taxation:

(a) the Collector shall have the same powers and remedies against the executors or administrators of such person, to the extent of the estate of such person in their hands, as he would have had against him in his lifetime;

(b) such executors or administrators shall make such returns as the Collector requires for the purpose of a full assessment;

(c) the assessment shall be made at the rates at which the tax ought to have been paid, and the amount payable shall be double the amount of the difference.

===== Page 168 =====
Between the tax so assessed and the amount actually paid by such person, and shall be a first charge on all the estate of such person which remains in the hands of the executors or administrators at the time when notice is given by the Collector to such executors or administrators that he proposes to make an assessment under this section and also on any part of the estate which may have already been distributed and have passed into the possession of a beneficiary. Such double taxation may be recovered in the manner provided by section 41 for the recovery of the tax and may be reduced or remitted in the manner provided by section 64;

(d) No lapse of time shall prevent the operation of this section, and the Collector may take all such proceedings and exercise all such powers and remedies for the purpose of giving effect to this section and recovering the double tax as in the case of ordinary assessments and taxations.

27. (1) Every person who is acting for another person or for a company or association in any of the capacities mentioned in sections 21, 22 and 23 shall declare to the Collector in writing signed by him the capacity in which he is so acting and the name, occupation and place of abode or business

(a) of such other person or of such company or association; and

(b) of any other person who is joined with him in acting in any such capacity.

(2) Every company or association which is acting for any person or for another company or association under section 21 or section 23 shall declare to the Collector in writing signed by its principal officer the name, occupation and place of abode or business of such person or such other company or association.

28. Every person who is chargeable in any capacity mentioned in sections 21, 22, 23, 24, 25 and every company or association which is chargeable under section 21 or section 23 may out of the moneys which he or it receives in that capacity retain the amount with which he or it is so chargeable.

F.—Indemnity to Employers, Trustees, Etc.

29. Every person who in pursuance of this Enactment deducts, retains or pays any tax in respect of the income of another person or of a company or association, and every company or association which pays any tax under section 21 or section 23 is hereby indemnified in respect of any claim by any person whomsoever for the deduction, retention or payment thereof.

PART V.

APPEAL FROM ASSESSMENT.

30. (1) Any person or principal officer who objects to the amount at which he or his company or association is assessed or denies that he or it is chargeable with the tax may petition the Commissioners hereinafter mentioned to reduce or cancel the assessment.

===== Page 169 =====
(2) The petition shall, as nearly as circumstances admit, be in the prescribed form and shall be filed as may be prescribed.

(3) The petition shall be presented within twenty-one days after receipt by the petitioner of a notification of assessment under section 20: Provided that the Commissioners may receive a petition after the expiration of that period if they are satisfied that the petitioner had sufficient cause for not presenting it within that period.

31. Notice in writing of the appeal together with a copy of the petition shall be served by the appellant upon the Collector within seven days after the presentation of the petition.

32. (1) The High Commissioner shall appoint a Board of Commissioners for each Division established under section 3 (hereinafter called "the Commissioners") for the purpose of hearing appeals from any assessment made by the Collector for such Division.

(2) Judges of the Supreme Court shall be ex-officio members of every such Board and at every meeting of any such Board a Judge of the Supreme Court shall be the Chairman.

(3) Appeals shall be heard by not less than three Commissioners, one of whom shall be a Judge of the Supreme Court, and shall be decided in accordance with the opinion of the majority of the Commissioners present: Provided that if there is no such majority, the assessment appealed from shall stand.

33. (1) The Commissioners shall fix a day and place for the hearing of the petition, and on the day and at the place so fixed or on the day and at the place, if any, to which they have adjourned, the hearing shall hear the petition and make such order thereon as they think fit.

Payment.

(2) The company, association or person chargeable with the assessment shall pay to the Collector the amount of the assessment determined by the order of the Commissioners within twenty-one days after such determination.

34. The Commissioners may, in order to determine how the petitioner or his company or association should be assessed, summon and enforce the attendance of witnesses and compel them to give evidence on affirmation and compel the production of documents by the same means and as far as possible in the same manner as is provided by any written law in respect of civil proceedings in the Supreme Court:

Provided that the Commissioners shall not call for any evidence except at the instance of the petitioner.

35. The Commissioners shall not upon the hearing of any such appeal cancel, or make any reduction in, the assessment made by the Collector unless it shall upon the hearing of such appeal appear to the majority of the Commissioners by examination of the petitioner upon affirmation or by other evidence to be produced by him, that he or his company or association is not liable to or has been overcharged by such assessment.

===== Page 170 =====
36. At the hearing of any appeal, the Collector may either personally or by counsel:
(a) attend during the entire time of hearing such appeal;
(b) cross-examine the petitioner and any witnesses produced by him;
(c) give his reasons in support of the assessment appealed against;
(d) produce evidence in support of such assessment.

37. At the hearing of any appeal, any advocate and solicitor of the Supreme Court shall be entitled to plead before the Commissioners either viva voce or by writing, and any accountant approved by the Federal Secretary shall be entitled to be heard by them on behalf of the petitioner or the Collector.

38. The provisions of the Evidence Enactment shall apply to any proceedings under this Part.

CASE FOR THE OPINION OF THE COURT OF APPEAL.

39. (1) The petitioner or the Collector, if dissatisfied with the determination of any appeal to the Commissioners as being erroneous in point of law, may within twenty-one days after the determination by notice in writing require the Commissioners to state and sign a case for the opinion of the Court of Appeal thereon, setting forth the facts and the determination.

(2) The party requiring the same shall within seven days after receiving the case so stated and signed transmit it to the Registrar of the Supreme Court, and shall at the same time, unless he has previously done so, send a copy of the case to the other party.

(3) In relation to cases so stated and the hearing thereof, the following provisions shall have effect:
(a) the Court of Appeal shall hear and determine the question or questions of law arising on a case transmitted under this section and may thereupon reverse, affirm or amend the determination of the Commissioners or remit the matter to the Commissioners with its opinion thereon or may make such other order in relation to the matter and, subject to sub-section (6) of this section, such order as to costs as it thinks fit;
(b) the Court of Appeal may cause the case to be sent back for amendment and thereupon the same shall be amended accordingly and judgment shall be deferred pending such amendment;
(c) a Judge sitting in chambers may exercise the powers conferred upon a Judge by section 15 of the Courts Enactment in connection with any such case.

(4) Any judgment or order of the Court of Appeal upon any case stated under this section shall be deemed, for the purposes of section 33 of the Courts Enactment, to be a judgment or order in a civil matter.

(5) Although a case so stated is pending before the Court of Appeal, the tax shall be paid according to the assessment of the Commissioners as if such case had not been required to be stated, and if the amount of the assessment is altered by the order or judgment of such Court, the difference in the amount,

===== Page 171 =====
If too much has been paid, it shall be repaid with such interest, if any, as such Court allows, and, if too little has been paid, shall be forthwith paid and may be recovered as if it were an arrear.

(6) In any case when the Collector appeals to the Court of Appeal or to the Privy Council, the costs of the respondent shall be taxed as between party and party and paid out of the general revenues of the Federated Malay States.

40. No suit shall lie in any Civil Court to set aside or modify any assessment made under this Enactment except as provided in this Part.

PART VI.

RECOVERY OF TAX.

41. (1) The tax chargeable under this Enactment shall be payable within the prescribed time.

(2) In case of default under this Enactment, the Collector may recover a sum not exceeding double the amount of the tax in the manner hereinafter provided.

(3) The Collector shall certify under his hand and seal the sum to be recovered under sub-section (2), and such sum shall thereupon be recoverable as though due on a decree issued in favour of the Government of the Federated Malay States against the defaulter. Proceedings for such recovery may be taken in the appropriate Court.

(4) The Collector shall file in the appropriate Court the certificate referred to in sub-section (3), whereupon the Court shall, upon his application, proceed to execution as if such certificate were a decree of the said Court.

(5) Where the defaulter is an association, any proceedings under this section may be taken against the principal officer of such association both in his personal capacity and on behalf of such association, and execution may be levied in the first place on the property of such association, or if the execution on such property does not produce a sufficient amount, then on the property of any persons who constitute such association.

PART VII.

MISCELLANEOUS.

42. When a company, association or person has more than one place of business or residence in different Divisions, the Collector-General may determine that it or he be assessed for the tax

(a) in each Division separately; or

(b) in one or more Divisions.

43. When any money is paid under this Enactment to the Collector or is recovered thereunder by him, he shall give a receipt for the same in the prescribed form.

44. If

(a) any person dies or is adjudged a bankrupt or is from any other specific cause deprived of or loses income or

===== Page 172 =====
(b) Any company, association or person ceases to carry on business, he or it or his or its representative in interest may apply to the Collector within nine months after the end of the year 1941, and the Collector, on proof to his satisfaction of any such cause as foresaid, shall amend the assessment as the case may require and refund such sum, if any, as has been overpaid.

45. (1) The Collector, on proof to his satisfaction that any sum paid as tax by deduction or otherwise under this Enactment
(a) was not liable to be paid, or
(b) was paid in excess of the amount which is liable to be paid, or
(c) was paid in error, shall on the application of the company, association or person charged with such tax made within nine months after the end of the year 1941 refund to it or him the whole amount paid or the amount paid in excess or in error.

(2) No relief under this Enactment which depends wholly or partially on the total income of any company, association or person shall be given to any company, association or person, unless it or he is resident or carries on business in the Federated Malay States or in a part of the British Empire where provision exists for imposing an income tax.

46. Where it appears to the Collector that any company, association or person chargeable with tax has not been assessed or has been assessed at less than the proper amount, the Collector may, at any time during the year 1941 or within three years after the expiration thereof, assess such company, association or person at the amount or additional amount at which according to his judgment such company, association or person ought to have been assessed, and the provisions of this Enactment as to notice of assessment, appeal and other proceedings shall apply to such assessment or additional assessment and to the tax charged thereunder:

Provided that where the non-assessment or under-assessment of any person is due to fraud or wilful evasion, such assessment or additional assessment may be made at any time within ten years after the expiration of the year 1941.

47. Every person when he is required so to do by notice from a Collector shall within the time specified in such notice prepare in accordance with the directions of such notice and deliver to the Collector a list signed by him containing to the best of his belief the proper name, occupation and place of business or employment of every lodger and inmate in his dwelling-house.

48. (1) Every agreement, contract, condition, or arrangement, either oral or in writing, made after the 1st day of August, 1939, between a landlord and a tenant of land which imposes or purports to impose upon the tenant liability for payment or for compensating the landlord for the payment of any tax upon the income derived from such land shall be void and of no effect.

(2) Where in pursuance of any such agreement, contract, condition or arrangement as mentioned in sub-section (1) any payment is made on or after the 1st day of January, 1941, by a tenant to his landlord or to the Collector, then the amount shall be recoverable from the landlord by the tenant by whom it was

===== Page 173 =====
made, and may without prejudice to any other method of recovery be deducted from any rent payable by him to the landlord.

49. Notwithstanding the provisions of any other written law, the Collector may give notice in writing to any officer of or in the employment of Government or of any body constituted or incorporated by any written law requiring him to furnish within the time limited by such notice any particulars which he may require for the purposes of this Enactment and which may be in the possession of such officer.

OFFENCES AND PENALTIES.

50. Any person guilty of an offence against this Enactment or any person who contravenes or fails to comply with any of the provisions of this Enactment or of any rules made thereunder, for which no penalty is specifically provided, shall be liable to a fine not exceeding five hundred dollars or to imprisonment for a term not exceeding six months.

51. Every person who
(a) fails to comply with the requirements of a notice given to him under this Enactment; or
(b) fails to attend in answer to a notice or summons issued to him under this Enactment or having attended fails without sufficient cause to answer any question lawfully put to him
shall be guilty of an offence and shall be liable to a fine not exceeding five hundred dollars or to imprisonment for a term not exceeding six months.

52. (1) Every person who without reasonable excuse
(a) makes an incorrect statement or return by omitting or understating any income or total income of which he is required by this Enactment to make a statement or return; or
(b) gives any incorrect information in relation to any matter or thing affecting his own liability to pay the tax or the liability of any other person or of any company or association to pay the tax
shall be guilty of an offence and shall be liable to a fine not exceeding double the amount of tax which has been undercharged in consequence of such incorrect statement, return, or information, or would have been so undercharged if the statement, return or information had been accepted as correct.

(2) No person shall be liable to any penalty under this section unless the complaint concerning such offence shall have been made before the 31st day of December, 1941.

(3) The Collector-General, with the concurrence of the Public Prosecutor, may compound any offence under this section or under section 50 or section 51, and may before judgment compound any proceedings thereunder.

53. (1) Any person who wilfully with intent to evade or to assist any other person to evade the tax imposed under this Enactment
(a) omits from a statement or return made under this Enactment any income or any part of any total income which should be included; or

===== Page 174 =====
(b) makes any false statement or entry in any return made under this Enactment; or

(c) makes any false statement in connection with a claim for a deduction or allowance; or

(d) signs any statement or return furnished under this Enactment without reasonable grounds for believing the same to be true; or

(e) gives any false answer whether orally or in writing to any question or request for information asked or made in accordance with the provisions of this Enactment; or

(f) prepares or maintains or authorises the preparation or maintenance of any false books of account or other records or falsifies or authorises the falsification of any books of account or records; or

(g) makes use of any fraud, art, or contrivance whatsoever or authorises the use of any such fraud, art, or contrivance shall be guilty of an offence, and shall for each such offence be liable to a fine not exceeding five thousand dollars and treble the amount of tax for which he is liable under this Enactment or to imprisonment for a term not exceeding two years, or to both such fine and imprisonment.

(2) The Collector-General, with the concurrence of the Public Prosecutor, may compound any offence under this section and may before judgment compound any proceedings thereunder.

54. The institution of proceedings for or the imposition of a penalty, fine, or term of imprisonment under this Enactment shall not relieve any person company or association from liability to payment of any tax for which he or it is or may be liable.

55. No prosecution in respect of any offence punishable under this Enactment shall be instituted without the sanction of the Public Prosecutor or a deputy of the Public Prosecutor.

56. (1) Any offence against this Enactment may be tried by the Court of a Magistrate and such Court may, notwithstanding anything in the Courts Enactment, award the full punishment with which such offence is punishable: Provided that the Public Prosecutor may in writing designate by which Court of a Magistrate any offence shall be tried.

(2) The provisions of this Enactment shall not affect any criminal proceedings under any other written law for the time being in force in the Federated Malay States.

57. Any proceeding under section 19 or Part V shall be deemed to be a judicial proceeding within the meaning of sections 193 and 228 of the Penal Code.

58. Where under this Enactment a duty is imposed on a company or an association, its principal officer shall be responsible for the performance of the duty and may be proceeded against for any offence against this Enactment.

59. Any company, association or person whose duty it is under this Enactment to deduct and to pay to the Collector the tax shall, if it or he fails to deduct or pay such tax to the

===== Page 175 =====
Collector within the prescribed time shall be deemed to be in default in respect of such tax, but without prejudice to any other consequences.

60. (1) Except in the performance of his duties under this Enactment, every person who has been appointed under or who is or has been employed in carrying out or in assisting any person to carry out the provisions of this Enactment shall preserve and aid in preserving secrecy with regard to all matters relating to the affairs of any person that may come to his knowledge in the performance of his duties under this Enactment, and shall not communicate any such matter to any person other than the person to whom such matter relates or his authorised representative, nor suffer or permit any person to have access to any records in the possession, custody or control of the Collector-General or any Collector: Provided that nothing in this section shall prevent any such person from answering or justify any such person in refraining from answering any question put to him by a police officer lawfully making any investigation in respect of any offence alleged to have been committed against this Enactment or from producing to any such officer any such records.

(2) Every person appointed under or employed in carrying out the provisions of this Enactment shall before acting under this Enactment take and subscribe before a Magistrate an affirmation of secrecy in the prescribed form.

(3) No person appointed under or employed in carrying out the provisions of this Enactment shall be required to produce in any Court any statement or return, document, or assessment, or to divulge or communicate to any Court any matter or thing coming under his notice in the performance of his duties under this Enactment, except as may be necessary for the purpose of carrying into effect the provisions of this Enactment.

(4) Notwithstanding anything contained in this section, the Collector-General or any Collector may communicate any matter which comes to his knowledge

(a) to any Collector of Stamp Duties or to the Collector or to any Assistant Collector of Estate Duty; or

(b) to the income tax authority of any part of the British Empire to such an extent as the Collector-General or Collector may deem necessary to enable the correct relief to be given from income tax in that part in respect of the payment of the tax imposed under this Enactment in the Federated Malay States; or

(c) to any Collector-General or Collector charged with the assessment and collection of income tax under any written law in force in the Colony or in any Unfederated Malay State.

(5) Notwithstanding anything contained in this section, the Collector-General or any Collector may permit the Auditor or the Accountant-General or any duly authorised officer in the Department of either of them to have such access to any records or documents as may be necessary for the performance of his

===== Page 176 =====
Official duties. The Auditor, the Accountant-General, or any duly authorised officer under this sub-section shall be deemed to be a person employed in carrying out the provisions of this Enactment for the purpose of sub-section (1).

(6) Any person who knowingly contravenes any of the provisions of this section shall be liable to a fine not exceeding one thousand dollars or to imprisonment for a term not exceeding six months.

SERVICE.

61. A notice under this Enactment may be served on the company, association, or person to which or whom it is addressed:

(a) by sending it through the post under registered cover addressed to it or him at the address given in its or his return or statement last delivered to the Collector or at the house at which it or he ordinarily carries on business or resides;

(b) by tendering or delivering it under cover to any principal officer of the company or association or the person to which or whom it may be addressed.

62. If no such address is known or if no such principal officer or person can be found, a notice may be served by affixing a copy of the notice on the outer door of the house in which the company, association, or person was last known ordinarily to carry on business or reside.

RULES.

63. (1) The High Commissioner may from time to time make rules generally for carrying out the provisions of this Enactment and for the ascertainment and determination of any class of income.

(2) Without prejudice to the generality of the foregoing power, such rules may:

(a) prescribe the manner in which and the procedure by which the total income, income, profits, and gains shall be arrived at in the case of:

(i) companies, associations, or persons carrying on business as bankers, insurers, or shipowners;

(ii) companies not incorporated in the Federated Malay States;

(b) provide for granting relief in cases where hardship would be caused by assessment to the full rate of tax appropriate to the total income;

(c) prescribe the procedure to be followed on application for refunds and reliefs;

(d) prescribe the time at or before which anything shall be done;

(e) provide for any matter which by this Enactment is to be or may be prescribed.

(3) In cases where total income or income, profits, and gains liable to tax cannot be definitely ascertained, the rules may prescribe methods by which an estimate of such income may be made and the proportion thereof liable to tax.

(4) Such rules may prescribe penalties for any contravention thereof or failure to comply therewith not exceeding in each case a sum of five hundred dollars.

===== Page 177 =====
(5) All rules made under this section shall be published in the Gazette and shall come into force upon such publication.

(6) All such rules shall be laid, as soon as conveniently may be, on the table of the Federal Council at a meeting of the Council, and the Council may thereupon by Resolution confirm, amend, alter or revoke any such rule with effect from the date of its publication in the Gazette under sub-section (5). Any such Resolution shall be published in the Gazette.

REDUCTION OR REMISSION OF TAX.

64. The Federal Council may by Resolution reduce or remit, whether prospectively or retrospectively, the whole or any part of the tax with which any company, association or person or class of companies, associations or persons is chargeable if the payment of such tax would cause undue hardship. Any such Resolution shall be published in the Gazette.

APPLICATION OF PROCEEDS.

65. The net amount of the tax received by the Collectors appointed under this Enactment after deduction of the expenses of and incidental to its assessment and collection, together with any fines and penalties imposed and paid under this Enactment, shall be applied to defraying the expenses incurred in the prosecution of the war and for no other purposes.
